  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a792b231-1da0-4363-b29a-2fd96ad425a7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText10505940352448228444" style="display:none">From a brilliant new voice in fantasy comes a band of heroes, a world in peril, and an unforgettable heroine whose unexpected gift of magic awakens an ancient, slumbering evil.<br /><br />On a fateful night five centuries ago, three made a desperate last stand, sacrificing everything to preserve the only hope of goodness in the beautiful, doomed land of Alasea. Now, on the anniversary of that ominous night, a girl-child ripens into the heritage of lost power. But before she can even comprehend her terrible new gift, the Dark Lord dispatches his winged monsters to capture her and bring him the embryonic magic she embodies.<br /><br />Fleeing the minions of darkness, Elena is swept toward certain doom-and into the company of unexpected allies. Aided by a one-armed warrior and a strange seer, she forms a band of the hunted and the cursed, the outcasts and the outlaws, to battle the unstoppable forces of evil and rescue a once-glorious empire...</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Definitely depends on the maturity of the reader. I would have read this in high school for sure, but that won't be the case for everyone. There are d<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Definitely depends on the maturity of the reader. I would have read this in high school for sure, but that won't be the case for everyone. There are definitely adult themes, but when it comes right down to it it's high fantasy and mostly about that. Generally speaking I would say maybe 16 and up, but again, depends on the reader.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_62992842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62992842" />
    <a title="Kate Cornett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2506828-kate-cornett"><img alt="Kate Cornett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1256331996p2/2506828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62992842?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Cornett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Cornett" href="/user/show/2506828-kate-cornett">Kate Cornett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506828-kate-cornett?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506828-kate-cornett?shelf=hot-lead-male">hot-lead-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2506828-kate-cornett?shelf=awesome-male-protagonist">awesome-male-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62992842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13694638275455006844">This is one of my favorite fantasy books of all time. I was stunned and completely entranced by the introduction of the story. It starts out in such a unique and impacting way, and then get's better and better. It is a page-turner for sure, making it extremely difficult to put down.<br/><br/>The characters are interesting, complex, and well thought-out. They definitely add to the reason why this is such a great book. There are some characters that I will never forget--Such as one of the heroes, Er'ril of </span>
  <span id="freeText13694638275455006844" style="display:none">This is one of my favorite fantasy books of all time. I was stunned and completely entranced by the introduction of the story. It starts out in such a unique and impacting way, and then get's better and better. It is a page-turner for sure, making it extremely difficult to put down.<br /><br />The characters are interesting, complex, and well thought-out. They definitely add to the reason why this is such a great book. There are some characters that I will never forget--Such as one of the heroes, Er'ril of Standi, whom I instantly fell in love and sympathized with. And of course, one of the villains, Greshym, whom is one of the most interesting and bad-ass dark wizards of all time in my opinion.<br /> <br />James Clemens' writing is superb. If your a writer, you might wish you could write as well as he does after you read this book.<br /><br />As for his fantasy world, it is definitely one that you can get sucked into and wish to be a part of. The lands he creates are magical and beautiful and, as always, insert beautiful pictures in your mind.<br /><br />The only thing I had a problem with in this book were all of the unnesessary aposthrephies. He uses them a lot in character names. Though they aren't distracting, I don't see why they need to be there most of the time.<br /><br />With that being said, this is a worthwhile book to check out. If you like this book, then you will most likely enjoy the rest in this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13694638275455006844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_60339290" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60339290" />
    <a title="Becka Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2424549-becka-sutton"><img alt="Becka Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245170605p2/2424549.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60339290?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becka Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becka Sutton" href="/user/show/2424549-becka-sutton">Becka Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who don't mind formulaic fantasy</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60339290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4727612676294896523">This book falls into a very unusual category for me. Books I don't especially like that I manage to finish. Since I only review books I finish this is one of the rare times you'll see a broadly negative review from me.<br/><br/>It took me two attempts. When I first bought it I tried to read it and gave up about a third of the way through. A few months later I uncovered it while tidying up and gave it another shot. This time I finished it, but I still wasn't entirely impressed.<br/><br/>This is Fantasy by the number</span>
  <span id="freeText4727612676294896523" style="display:none">This book falls into a very unusual category for me. Books I don't especially like that I manage to finish. Since I only review books I finish this is one of the rare times you'll see a broadly negative review from me.<br /><br />It took me two attempts. When I first bought it I tried to read it and gave up about a third of the way through. A few months later I uncovered it while tidying up and gave it another shot. This time I finished it, but I still wasn't entirely impressed.<br /><br />This is Fantasy by the numbers in the worst possible way. Dark Lords, near human races, innocent protagonist with strange powers they didn't ask for and don't want, wise councillors, evil monsters - how many times have I read this story under other titles and names? Enough that I'd like to see something different for once.<br /><br />The characters are interesting enough and there is good dose of plot tension in spite of the clicheness of the story - Clemens even pulled off a couple of surprises but the ending and most of the "twists" were predictable. And for some reason beyond the cliches and the predictability it grated on me. This I suspect is a personal foible, so if you don't mind formulaic fantasy this might float your boat.<br /><br />I won't be buying the rest of series though. Two stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4727612676294896523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2120092104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120092104" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71147186-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514980922p2/71147186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120092104?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/71147186-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8177006-wit-ch-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71147186-justine?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71147186-justine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120092104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16451641115257271501">I read this book for the first time 8 years ago. I was new to the Fantasy genre, quite young and loved it absolutely. So much so that I bought the four remaining volumes and read them all back to back. So I was a bit afraid not to love it as much this time. What if I realize it's not good at all? I have so fond memories of this series! <br/><br/>Fortunately, I loved it as much as the first time!<br/><br/>Where to begin? <br/>Maybe with the only "flaw": it's a slow book, at least, it was to me. Everything builds slowly t</span>
  <span id="freeText16451641115257271501" style="display:none">I read this book for the first time 8 years ago. I was new to the Fantasy genre, quite young and loved it absolutely. So much so that I bought the four remaining volumes and read them all back to back. So I was a bit afraid not to love it as much this time. What if I realize it's not good at all? I have so fond memories of this series! <br /><br />Fortunately, I loved it as much as the first time!<br /><br />Where to begin? <br />Maybe with the only "flaw": it's a slow book, at least, it was to me. Everything builds slowly to get to the end. But it's not really a flaw: I was impatient because I already read the book and knew where we were heading. And I wanted to get there quickly to start the real journey! <br /><br />The best part of this re-read was getting back to the characters and picturing the scenes just like the first time. It's like I got back to friends and familiar places: it was great! When we get to the orchard, I didn't have to make an effort to instantanely picture the trees, the valley, Elena and Joach! Same for the forests, the village, the roads or anything really! <br />Getting back to the characters was a delight. I really love them all, except one of them: I just can't bear Mogweed. Really, I can't. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Not because he is evil - I actually like Rockingham: I find his story really moving when we finally understand what happened to him! But, Mogweed. He is just a coward and egocentric. He can't think of others, he only thinks of himself, his life, his safety. He is ready to sacrifice his own twin to get what he wants. It's just wrong. I really hate him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> My favorite characters are probably Nee'lahn and Kral. They particularly move me. She is small and wants nobody to see her, she wants to melt in the setting, to stay invisible around people. But when she has something to say to her friends, she does without hesitation. She is fierce, she is brave, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her connection to the forest is just so beautiful. I love that she is a nyphai and hates that people call her people "nymph". I loved the first scene, when she sings and discovers Er'ril. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Kral is the opposite of Nee'lahn: male, mountain man, big and assertive. But he is also very touching. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was so moved by the scene when he thinks he lies and can't get rid of the shame of it! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But just like her, Kral is brave and won't back from a fight to save his friends. <br />I also love the other characters: Tol'chuk moves me too, he is close to Kral in my heart, and I was surprised by the love I felt for him the first time I read the book, because I never encountered an <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[o'gre <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> like him and loved him; Fardale, how can I not love him? I mean, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he is a wolf, he is brave, ready to protect a man he "should" hate, Mogweed, ready to kill him or let him die. He puts up with Mogweed: eternal respect, man! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>; Elena, of course, even if she's not my favorite character, probably because she is a child here and can't do anything on her own, needing others - which is normal, it's not a criticism - and so is not really on the forefront. Well, sometimes, she is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[we get in her head and we get to see her powers. She is impressive, and the reader can't wait for her to become a woman, the wit'ch, and to let the child behind. But can we really expect her to grow this quick when she is so young in this first book? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Er'ril ... I didn't remember he was sexist! But he is. Because of the way magic was in his time: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[only for men. Women couldn't be chosen by Chi. And I loooooooooooooved Bol's explanation for the fact that there is only one wit'ch when there were many wielders of Chi. I love the way Bol sees women and male as equals, when Er'ril is sure men/Chi are stronger, and so that the wit'ch's magic is weaker. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I still loved him: for his despair, his loss of hope, and his growing affection <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[for Elena. After the shock and horror, he wants to protect her. He becomes her Guardian, and I was moved once more! The scenes when he takes her in his arms to help her focus, the scene when he sees her, truly sees her, the scenes when we discover his despair because of what he's done centuries ago, the fact that he is haunted still by the boy he killed, the fact that he is redeemed, the fact that he is disabled - I never read a Fantasy book before with a disabled character! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I'm not clear or coherent here, I just love them all!<br />And that's also something I love with this series: it's diverse and original. We don't follow ordinary characters - even if Er'ril sometimes was a bit stereotypical maybe. They are from diverse backgrounds, different races, and they sometimes have something special: Er'ril and Tol'chuk for instance! <br /><br />I also love the fact that there is an inserted story in this series: a narrator tells us the story. We don't know who he is for the time being and he doesn't interrumpt the tale while he is telling it, but he'll push the reader to keep reading with some sentences like: "I have no more ink and no more heart for tonight to keep telling"! Thank you man, let's go grab book 2 then! <br /><br />This book was the first I read where there were some awful scenes and creatures: skaltum, gore, blood, monsters, darkness, WORMS. Why do authors put worms like these in their books? What is it with worms? I don't understand!! I still loved the world and wanted to get more, to re-discover more! I had forgotten some things, and it was great to read them anew! <br /><br />I didn't remember the ending, it got back to me while I was reading it! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Of course, if Greshym is alive, Shorkan is too! But I don't remember the confrontation of the brothers... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So, it was a great read, both because of nostalgia and because this book is genuinely good for me! Can't wait to go on with my reread! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16451641115257271501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2338459225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2338459225" />
    <a title="Ariana Fae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29984848-ariana-fae"><img alt="Ariana Fae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451784114p2/29984848.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338459225?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariana Fae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariana Fae" href="/user/show/29984848-ariana-fae">Ariana Fae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/29221597-wit-ch-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338459225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7095130180383323320">I read WIT'CH FIRE when it was first published in 1998 and loved it. I decided to listen to the audio version while on a flight to England, to see if after 20 years if I would feel the same. The answer is a definite yes. <br/> <br/>Clemens' spin on witches, dryads, trolls, elves, and the world he created was interesting. One thing I admire Clemens/Rollins for is his ability to create strong and interesting female characters like Elena. Granted Elena doesn't start off as a strong woman but a young girl on </span>
  <span id="freeText7095130180383323320" style="display:none">I read WIT'CH FIRE when it was first published in 1998 and loved it. I decided to listen to the audio version while on a flight to England, to see if after 20 years if I would feel the same. The answer is a definite yes. <br /> <br />Clemens' spin on witches, dryads, trolls, elves, and the world he created was interesting. One thing I admire Clemens/Rollins for is his ability to create strong and interesting female characters like Elena. Granted Elena doesn't start off as a strong woman but a young girl on the brink of womanhood, uncertain, afraid, and dealing with a gift/curse she has no understanding of. However Clemens shows us there is a core of strength within Elena that eventually will be tempered. That's one of the reasons I loved this story. The supporting cast of characters, which is pretty diverse, helping Elena on her journey were interesting. I didn't realize the first time I read the book that they actually added to the world building, letting me see the land of Alasea from their eyes and experiences. It was clever way of doing it without info dumping. The magic system is original and unique, especially Elena's power. The story was also more enjoyable since it was narrated by Jennifer Van Dyck who did a wonderful job with all the voices. <br /><br />WIT'CH FIRE was a great revisit and it made me want to listen to the other books in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7095130180383323320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1517728927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1517728927" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4108709-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483512739p2/4108709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1517728927?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/4108709-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1517728927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5326479071324407967">I had to debate a lot between two and three stars, but I'm coming down on the side of two.<br/><br/>Clemens has a pretty beautiful story here, and there are some very interesting races and characters. The plot itself is actually pretty involving, except for the how familiar as it feels to fleeing the shire because of the Nazgul errr I mean fleeing the village because of the Ra'zak errr I mean fleeing the village because of the Skal-tum (Talk about recycled!)<br/><br/>The novel suffers though under two things:<br/><br/>1. An </span>
  <span id="freeText5326479071324407967" style="display:none">I had to debate a lot between two and three stars, but I'm coming down on the side of two.<br /><br />Clemens has a pretty beautiful story here, and there are some very interesting races and characters. The plot itself is actually pretty involving, except for the how familiar as it feels to fleeing the shire because of the Nazgul errr I mean fleeing the village because of the Ra'zak errr I mean fleeing the village because of the Skal-tum (Talk about recycled!)<br /><br />The novel suffers though under two things:<br /><br />1. An absolute deluge of characters. I'm serious, the entire book is filled with introducing characters. Since I was a kid I have always read three or four books at the same time, but the sheer number of introductions in this novel made this one hard to follow along with. Sick of the author introducing a new character at every major plot point? He will step it up by introducing two at a time, then splitting them up. Read this with a pad of paper, you're going to need it!<br /><br />2. Sticking an apostrophe into names doesn't make them different. The Dw'arfs, the El'vin, and the Og'res are all still completely recognizable, and the gimmick of apostrophes doesn't add ANYTHING to Wit'ch Fire.<br /><br /><br />I meant it when I said there is a wonderful plot buried in here to get through. I love the Chiric magic system, I love the dichotomy of light and dark, and I especially like the story of the Og're. It is some work to get through it though, and I can't say that it would be of average enjoyment to the average casual reader, hence the two stars.<br /><br />I'm up in the air about the sequels... we will just have to see how my "To Read" list progresses.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5326479071324407967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81173460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4752740139411982029">I agree with both the positive and negative reviews on this one.<br/>It was captivating, or I wouldn't have bothered finishing it.<br/> I liked several of the characters or at least found them compelling.<br/>I was REALLY bothered by the awkward, stiff dialogue and a few writing-tics the author has, such as needing to emphasize a point by repeating it. ("He found himself completely immobilized. He could not move." Like that. Grrrrrrrrrr!) I will be continuing with the series, though, because I am particularly </span>
  <span id="freeText4752740139411982029" style="display:none">I agree with both the positive and negative reviews on this one.<br />It was captivating, or I wouldn't have bothered finishing it.<br /> I liked several of the characters or at least found them compelling.<br />I was REALLY bothered by the awkward, stiff dialogue and a few writing-tics the author has, such as needing to emphasize a point by repeating it. ("He found himself completely immobilized. He could not move." Like that. Grrrrrrrrrr!) I will be continuing with the series, though, because I am particularly drawn to the idea of a destructive book of power, and a young woman coming into her dangerous powers and not being just 100 percent altruistic about using them. Yes, Elena has to save everybody's collective butts, but she actually ENJOYS the feel of power, of making her enemies hurt, watching the baddies squirm. That adds a note of complexity that makes me want to keep going and see if Clemens gets more comfortable writing dialogue.<br /></span>

          </span>

    <a title="Nathalia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4049771-nathalia"><img alt="Nathalia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596275153p2/4049771.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113147402?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4049771-nathalia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113147402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2460451761895121389">I absolutely loved this series. What first caught my attention was not just the vast amount of characters in each novel, but also the wonderful characterization and the beautiful world building. However, if you have a terrible memory with names or if you just have a difficult time remembering what ability each character possesses, then I would move swiftly along. <br/><br/>I give this novel and the series 5/5. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2562244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10388461939983282684">This is not good, and you shouldn't read it. The plot was lacking in originality, but honestly my main problem was with the author's writing. And the bizarre tendency to insert apostrophies in the middle of words in order to make them exotic (that's my best guess, in any case). This series is comparable to a badly written romance series. Fantasy trash. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94985372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94985372" />
    <a title="Shera (Book Whispers)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3167178-shera-book-whispers"><img alt="Shera (Book Whispers)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446841556p2/3167178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94985372?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shera (Book Whispers)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shera (Book Whispers)" href="/user/show/3167178-shera-book-whispers">Shera (Book Whispers)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=epic-and-high-fantasy">epic-and-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3167178-shera-book-whispers?shelf=90s">90s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94985372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11429194358940194190">Thoughts:<br/><br/>This book had a really fun beginning. Showing that the book we are about to read is a history of how the old world ended, and that it is nothing but lies. Promising, right? How many fantasy books start off like that? Not many so I was really excited to start out.<br/><br/>Within 20 pages, nothing big really popped out. The reader has read the prologue that gives us some history, and we're rushing on to meet our young heroine. Who is just coming into her powers and is now a hunted girl because of </span>
  <span id="freeText11429194358940194190" style="display:none">Thoughts:<br /><br />This book had a really fun beginning. Showing that the book we are about to read is a history of how the old world ended, and that it is nothing but lies. Promising, right? How many fantasy books start off like that? Not many so I was really excited to start out.<br /><br />Within 20 pages, nothing big really popped out. The reader has read the prologue that gives us some history, and we're rushing on to meet our young heroine. Who is just coming into her powers and is now a hunted girl because of them.<br /><br />I've read a lot of fantasy books, and it's only natural to hit the same story over and over again. The thing with good fantasy books if they don't have a new idea, then the author takes the same old tale and spices it up. Spices it up by the writing style, characters and how they interact, and so many little factors. This book didn't really have any of that.<br /><br />After 175 pages I can confidently say this book has solid writing, really good and descriptive. However, after that many pages all of the characters introduced, and still being introduced, I just couldn't connect with them. I was not interested in them, I could profile all of them in to standard fantasy character catergories. For all of the great writing, the characters never developed. I know it takes time for you to connect to the characters especially when some are still be introduced. After 175 pages, there should be some characters you care about, the author should be able to make you want to know the new ones. <br /><br />After 175 pages, nothing new was being added to the plot and I was bored. Book Boredom is a rare thing that I have rarely visited, and quite frankly don't like to stay in too long. So out of self preservation, I stopped.<br /><br />Then picked it up again and tried last week to read it. Maybe I wasn't in the mood (which can some times happen with fantasy), maybe I just didn't read enough, and so many other excuses.<br /><br />First off no matter the fantasy book, or how many times the same old tale is being told. It should still give you something to make it new.<br /><br />175-200 pages should be more then enough time to connect with a book, if it takes more the author is not doing their job.<br /><br /><br />Bottom Line:<br /><br />This book had a great beginning and fantastic writing. Swiftly it falls into the standard fantasy plot and it doesn't distinguish itself from the other books out there. I found myself not caring about the characters. After 175 pages Book Boredom set in hard, and trying to pick it up again after starting did not cure it. For long term fantasy fans, stay away from this one. New fantasy adventurers, there's better things out there. <br /><br />Sexual Content:<br /><br />Nothing within a 175 pages, not even a kiss. <br /><br />Rating: <br /><br />1/5 –Couldn't even finish it, or wish I hadn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11429194358940194190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_163631096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163631096" />
    <a title="Emilie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4046576-emilie"><img alt="Emilie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163631096?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emilie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emilie" href="/user/show/4046576-emilie">Emilie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4046576-emilie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4046576-emilie?shelf=witches">witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163631096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer707885720761913076">I'm not a reader of this kind of high fantasy (epic?), the only other series I can link this one to is The Lord of the Rings by Tolkien... it says a lot about my high fantasy culture *lol*. But I truly <b>loved</b> reading it.<br/>Just like in TLR, we have a long and perilous quest to deliver the world of darkness, a bunch of different but allied characters, mythical creatures and of course a young hero/heroine whose destiny is bound with their world's fate.<br/><br/>But Wit'ch Fire has two things that Tolkien's saga</span>
  <span id="freeText707885720761913076" style="display:none">I'm not a reader of this kind of high fantasy (epic?), the only other series I can link this one to is The Lord of the Rings by Tolkien... it says a lot about my high fantasy culture *lol*. But I truly <b>loved</b> reading it.<br />Just like in TLR, we have a long and perilous quest to deliver the world of darkness, a bunch of different but allied characters, mythical creatures and of course a young hero/heroine whose destiny is bound with their world's fate.<br /><br />But Wit'ch Fire has two things that Tolkien's saga doesn't have:<br />- Not too many descriptive passages... maybe not enough? Let's face it, TLR and especially The Fellowship of the Ring has a lot of descriptions. That's the reason, it took me so long to get into that book but once I was into it, I couldn't stop reading. That's not a problem in James Clemens' novel so the reading is fast-paced which is quite nice.<br />- An excessive amount of apostrophes. It is a bit distracting at first but I quickly got used to it. It's an aesthetic choice like any other.<br /><br />Wit'ch Fire is a fast-paced, action-packed, gripping, surprising, exciting novel... yes, I did say I loved it XD<br />The characters are well-defined, complex and captivating. For once, there wasn't a character that annoyed me, not even Elena. For a 13 years old girl who has her life turned totally upside down, she takes it rather well compared to other heroines.<br /><br />The other thing I appreciated about that book is that it doesn't end in a cliffhanger so even if you don't have the following installment it won't make you crazy. I've already ordered the rest of the novels but I can survive until they arrive lol.<br /><br />To summarize: Awesome, brilliant, must-be-read! Even if usually you're not a reader of this genre, give it a try. TOTALLY RECOMMENDED.</span>
  <a data-text-id="707885720761913076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Travis Simmons" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Travis Simmons" href="/user/show/7554875-travis-simmons">Travis Simmons</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7554875-travis-simmons?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer729694714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6288370290539449321">I read this book years ago (so many I don't want to count them) and loved it. I had read the second book as well, but couldn't remember if I got any further than that. I decided to go back and give it a chance again, from the beginning, so that I could read it in its entirety.<br/><br/>I am glad I did. It was still very enjoyable. There were a couple complaints, but not anything to do with the storyline or the writing. Well, a little to do with the writing, but not much. One was description, while it was </span>
  <span id="freeText6288370290539449321" style="display:none">I read this book years ago (so many I don't want to count them) and loved it. I had read the second book as well, but couldn't remember if I got any further than that. I decided to go back and give it a chance again, from the beginning, so that I could read it in its entirety.<br /><br />I am glad I did. It was still very enjoyable. There were a couple complaints, but not anything to do with the storyline or the writing. Well, a little to do with the writing, but not much. One was description, while it was very colorful and helped me envision the scene's beautifully, I think at times it was overdone. The other thing was Elena being so weak, which I'm sure changes. Of course, you have to remember that she is just a child, coming into adulthood, so when you put it into that perspective, it's all good.<br /><br />It starts out with an invading force to the land, and a plot to destroy it. However, with magick having left the lands, the wizards can only do one thing: create a book that will bring about a prophesied wit'ch. Skip forward a few hundred years and we meet Elena, a girl with a rose red hand, who is able to do some pretty strange things when she lets her mind wander. Danger, death, and intrigue follow Elena on her quest, and she meets up with some pretty awesome (and well built) races along the way.<br /><br />All in all, a good book, check it out! You won't be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6288370290539449321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer86265036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3007106709978511332">A creative combination of mythical creatures adapted to fit James Clemens Wit'ch Fire. Heartpounding action and suspense keep you hanging onto every last word. I didn't like the way that Clemens jumped from this character to that character especially when something unexpected happens. The gruesome and vivid descriptions allow the readers to become more engaged to the plot.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

I think this was his first book, and now he writes as James Rollins.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j4lbfetKbuO6qJo243cbpU/SvzTlS73tRlKXhdaosbK1BBeodZbijR4pCcXYDB3AZ3En28JzxO3Q4Vf9AJhhbw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fR2+QLMLssRNkbUSqbWZGK1lSHAFoXDU0jAzaw7w+gtHkPKVLdc+qukQJuGSzp99hcbQnyKZCdREg/MT2MAq1g==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer857231643313123842">James Clemens [Aka James Rollins] was born in Chicago, Illinois in 1961. With his three brothers and three sisters, he was raised in the Midwest and rural Canada. He attended the University of Missouri and graduated with a doctorate in veterinary medicine in 1985. The lure of ocean, sun, and new horizons eventually drew him to the West Coast, where he established his veterinary practice in Sacrame</span>
  <span id="freeText857231643313123842" style="display:none">James Clemens [Aka James Rollins] was born in Chicago, Illinois in 1961. With his three brothers and three sisters, he was raised in the Midwest and rural Canada. He attended the University of Missouri and graduated with a doctorate in veterinary medicine in 1985. The lure of ocean, sun, and new horizons eventually drew him to the West Coast, where he established his veterinary practice in Sacramento, California, eventually settling for good in the Sierra Nevada Mountains.<br /><br />He is the author of The Banned and the Banished series (The Wit’ch War Saga) and The Godslayer Chronicles.</span>
